				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix_Inc.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Netflix Inc.">Netflix Inc.</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the media service. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Netflix_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Netflix (disambiguation)">Netflix (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>Netflix, Inc.</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is an American <a href="/wiki/Over-the-top_media_service" title="Over-the-top media service">media-services provider</a> and <a href="/wiki/Production_company" title="Production company">production company</a> headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Los_Gatos,_California" title="Los Gatos, California">Los Gatos, California</a>, founded in 1997 by <a href="/wiki/Reed_Hastings" title="Reed Hastings">Reed Hastings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marc_Randolph" title="Marc Randolph">Marc Randolph</a> in <a href="/wiki/Scotts_Valley,_California" title="Scotts Valley, California">Scotts Valley, California</a>. The company's primary business is its subscription-based <a href="/wiki/Streaming_service_provider" title="Streaming service provider">streaming service</a> which offers online streaming of a library of films and television programs, including those produced in-house.<sup id="cite_ref-NYFLIX_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYFLIX-11">[11]</a></sup> As of April 2019, Netflix had over 148 million paid subscriptions worldwide, including 60 million in the United States, and over 154 million subscriptions total including free trials.<sup id="cite_ref-NFLX_Q1_2019_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NFLX_Q1_2019-12">[12]</a></sup> It is available worldwide except in mainland China (due to local restrictions), Syria, North Korea, and Crimea (due to U.S. sanctions). The company also has offices in India, Netherlands, Brazil, Japan, and South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Netflix is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Motion_Picture_Association_of_America" title="Motion Picture Association of America">Motion Picture Association</a> (MPA).

data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> US$7.582 billion (2019)<sup id="cite_ref-ir.netflix.com_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ir.netflix.com-7">[7]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th <li><a href="/wiki/StoryBots" title="StoryBots">StoryBots</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">URL</th><td class="url"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.netflix.com/">www<wbr></wbr>.netflix<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Alexa_Internet" title="Alexa Internet">Alexa</a> rank</th><td><img alt="Steady" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Steady" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> 20 <span style="font-size:85%;"><span class="nowrap">(March 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>)</span></span><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Registration</th><td>Required</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Registered_user" title="Registered user">Users</a></th><td>169 million (paid) <sup id="cite_ref-ir.netflix.com_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ir.netflix.com-7">[7]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Netflix's initial business model included <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a> sales and rental by mail, but Hastings abandoned the sales about a year after the company's founding to focus on the initial DVD rental business.<sup id="cite_ref-NYFLIX_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYFLIX-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-14">[14]</a></sup> Netflix expanded its business in 2010 with the introduction of streaming media while retaining the DVD and Blu-ray rental business. The company expanded internationally in 2010 with streaming available in Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> followed by Latin America and the Caribbean. Netflix entered the content-production industry in 2013, debuting its first series <i>House of Cards</i>.
</p><p>Since 2012, Netflix has taken more of an active role as producer and distributor for both film and television series, and to that end, it offers a variety of "<a href="/wiki/List_of_original_programs_distributed_by_Netflix" title="List of original programs distributed by Netflix">Netflix Original</a>" content through its online library.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> By January 2016, Netflix services operated in more than 190 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Netflix released an estimated 126 <a href="/wiki/Original_series" title="Original series">original series</a> and films in 2016, more than any other network or cable channel.<sup id="cite_ref-hr-backlash_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hr-backlash-18">[18]</a></sup> Their efforts to produce new content, secure the rights for additional content, and diversify through 190 countries have resulted in the company racking up billions in debt: $21.9 billion as of September 2017, up from $16.8 billion from the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> $6.5 billion of this is long-term debt, while the remaining is in long-term obligations.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In October 2018, Netflix announced it would raise another $2 billion in debt to help fund new content.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p><p>As of March 2020, Netflix offered just under 3,000 film titles for streaming on its U.S. service.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> This does not include multi-episode titles (series).
</p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Netflix" title="Timeline of Netflix">Timeline of Netflix</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Technical_details_of_Netflix" title="Technical details of Netflix">Technical details of Netflix</a></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Establishment"><span id="Founding_and_establishment"></span>Establishment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Establishment" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r923042769/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption-center{text-align:center;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:417px;max-width:417px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:201px;max-width:201px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:132px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:100_Winchester_Circle.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/100_Winchester_Circle.jpg/199px-100_Winchester_Circle.jpg" decoding="async" width="199" height="133" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 199px;height: 133px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/100_Winchester_Circle.jpg/199px-100_Winchester_Circle.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="199" data-height="133"> </span></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Netflix's longtime Los Gatos headquarters location and current legal address at 100 Winchester Circle (Building A)</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:212px;max-width:212px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:132px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:101_Albright_Way.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/101_Albright_Way.jpg/210px-101_Albright_Way.jpg" decoding="async" width="210" height="133" data-file-width="5024" data-file-height="3188"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 210px;height: 133px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/101_Albright_Way.jpg/210px-101_Albright_Way.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="210" data-height="133"> </span></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Netflix's Los Gatos headquarters expansion campus at 90 to 160 Albright Way (Building G, 101 Albright Way).<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Netflix was founded on August 29, 1997, in <a href="/wiki/Scotts_Valley,_California" title="Scotts Valley, California">Scotts Valley, California</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Marc_Randolph" title="Marc Randolph">Marc Randolph</a><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Reed_Hastings" title="Reed Hastings">Reed Hastings</a>. Randolph worked as a marketing director for Hastings' company, <a href="/wiki/Pure_Software" title="Pure Software">Pure Atria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Randolph was a co-founder of MicroWarehouse, a computer mail order company, and was later employed by <a href="/wiki/Borland_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Borland International">Borland International</a> as vice president of marketing. Hastings, a computer scientist and mathematician, sold Pure Atria to Rational Software Corporation in 1997 for $700 million in what was then the biggest acquisition in Silicon Valley history. They came up with the idea for Netflix while commuting between their homes in Santa Cruz and Pure Atria's headquarters in Sunnyvale while waiting for government regulators to approve the merger,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-28">[28]</a></sup> although Hastings has given several different explanations for how the idea was created.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p><p>Hastings invested $2.5 million in startup cash for Netflix.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-14">[14]</a></sup> Randolph admired the fledgling e-commerce company <a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a> and wanted to find a large category of portable items to sell over the Internet using a similar model. They considered and rejected VHS tapes as too expensive to stock and too delicate to ship. When they heard about DVDs, which were first introduced in the United States on March 24, 1997,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> they tested the concept of selling or renting DVDs by mail, by mailing a compact disc to Hastings' house in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_California" title="Santa Cruz, California">Santa Cruz</a>. When the disc arrived intact, they decided to take on the $16 billion home video sales and rental industry.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-28">[28]</a></sup> Hastings is often quoted saying that he decided to start Netflix after being fined $40 at a Blockbuster store for being late to return a copy of <i><a href="/wiki/Apollo_13_(film)" title="Apollo 13 (film)">Apollo 13</a>.</i> But this is an apocryphal story that he and Randolph designed to explain the company's business model and motivation.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-28">[28]</a></sup></p><p>Netflix launched as the world's first online DVD rental store, with only 30 employees and 925 titles available, which was almost the entire catalogue of DVDs in print at the time,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> through the pay-per-rent model with rates and due dates that were similar to its bricks-and-mortar rival, <a href="/wiki/Blockbuster_LLC" title="Blockbuster LLC">Blockbuster</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Membership_fee.2C_Blockbuster_acquisition_offer.2C_growth_start"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership_fee,_Blockbuster_acquisition_offer,_growth_start">Membership fee, Blockbuster acquisition offer, growth start</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Membership fee, Blockbuster acquisition offer, growth start" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Netflix introduced the monthly subscription concept in September 1999,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> and then dropped the single-rental model in early 2000. Since that time (see <a href="/wiki/Technical_details_of_Netflix" title="Technical details of Netflix">Technical details of Netflix</a>), the company has built its reputation on the business model of flat-fee unlimited rentals without due dates, late fees, shipping and handling fees, or per-title rental fees.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p><p>In 2000, when Netflix had just about 300,000 subscribers and relied on the U.S. Postal Service for the delivery of their DVDs, they were losing money and offered to be acquired by <a href="/wiki/Blockbuster_LLC" title="Blockbuster LLC">Blockbuster</a> for $50 million. They proposed that Netflix, which would be renamed as Blockbuster.com, would handle the online business, while Blockbuster would take care of the DVDs, making them less dependent on the U.S. Postal Service. The offer was declined.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p><p>While they experienced fast growth in early 2001, both the <a href="/wiki/Dot-com_bubble" title="Dot-com bubble">dot-com bubble</a> burst and the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> would occur later that year, affecting the company badly and forcing them to lay off one-third of their 120 employees. However, sales of DVD players finally took off as they became more affordable, selling for about $200 around Thanksgiving time, becoming one of that year's most popular Christmas gifts. By early 2002, Netflix saw a huge increase in their subscription business.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p><p>Netflix initiated an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> (IPO) on May 29, 2002, selling 5.5 million shares of <a href="/wiki/Common_stock" title="Common stock">common stock</a> at the price of <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>15.00 per share. On June 14, 2002, the company sold an additional 825,000 shares of common stock at the same price. After incurring substantial losses during its first few years, Netflix posted its first profit during the fiscal year 2003, earning US$6.5 million profit on revenues of US$272 million. In 2005, 35,000 different films were available, and Netflix shipped 1 million DVDs out every day.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p><p>Randolph, a dominant producer and board member for Netflix, retired from the company in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p><p>Netflix was sued in 2004 for false advertising in relation to claims of "unlimited rentals" with "one-day delivery".<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Video_on_demand_introduction.2C_declining_DVD_sales.2C_global_expansion"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_on_demand_introduction,_declining_DVD_sales,_global_expansion">Video on demand introduction, declining DVD sales, global expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Video on demand introduction, declining DVD sales, global expansion" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r923042769/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:189px;max-width:189px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:187px;max-width:187px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:NFOrg.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/NFOrg.png/185px-NFOrg.png" decoding="async" width="185" height="80" data-file-width="319" data-file-height="138"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 185px;height: 80px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/NFOrg.png/185px-NFOrg.png" data-alt="" data-width="185" data-height="80"> </span></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">First logo, used from 1997 to 2000</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:187px;max-width:187px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Netflix_logo.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Netflix_logo.svg/185px-Netflix_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="185" height="86" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="464"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 185px;height: 86px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Netflix_logo.svg/185px-Netflix_logo.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="185" data-height="86" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Netflix_logo.svg/278px-Netflix_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Netflix_logo.svg/370px-Netflix_logo.svg.png 2x"> </span></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Netflix logo used from 2000 to 2014</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>For some time, the company had considered offering movies online, but it was only in the mid-2000s that data speeds and bandwidth costs had improved sufficiently to allow customers to download movies from the net. The original idea was a "Netflix box" that could download movies overnight, and be ready to watch the next day. By 2005, they had acquired movie rights and designed the box and service, and were ready to go public with it. But after discovering YouTube, and witnessing how popular streaming services were despite the lack of high-definition content, the concept of using a hardware device was scrapped and replaced with a streaming concept instead, a project that was completed in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p><p>Netflix developed and maintains an extensive personalized video-recommendation system based on ratings and reviews by its customers. On October 1, 2006, Netflix offered a <a href="/wiki/Netflix_Prize" title="Netflix Prize">$1,000,000 prize</a> to the first developer of a video-recommendation <a href="/wiki/Algorithm" title="Algorithm">algorithm</a> that could beat its existing algorithm Cinematch, at predicting customer ratings by more than 10%.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2007, the company delivered its billionth DVD,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> and began to move away from its original core business model of DVDs, by introducing <a href="/wiki/Video_on_demand" title="Video on demand">video on demand</a> via the Internet. Netflix grew as DVD sales fell from 2006 to 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p><p>Another contributing factor for the company's online DVD rental success was that they could offer a much larger selection of movie titles to choose from than Blockbuster's rental outlets. But when they started to offer streaming content for free to its subscribers in 2007, it could offer no more than about 1000 movies and TV-shows, just 1% compared to its more than 100,000 different DVD titles. Yet as the popularity kept growing, the number of titles available for streaming was increasing as well and had reached 12,000 movies and shows in June 2009. One of the key things about Netflix was that it had a recommendation system known as cinematch, which not only got viewers to remain attached to the service, by creating a switching cost, but it also brought out those movies which were underrated so that customers could view those movies too from their recommendations. This was an attribute that not only benefited Netflix but also benefited its viewers and those studios which were minor compared to others.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2013, Netflix reported that it had added two million United States customers during the fourth quarter of 2012, with a total of 27.1 million United States streaming customers, and 29.4 million total streaming customers. In addition, revenue was up 8% to $945 million for the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wired-2485033_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wired-2485033-50">[50]</a></sup> That number increased to 36.3 million subscribers (29.2 million in the United States) in April 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-news.yahoo.com_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.yahoo.com-51">[51]</a></sup> As of September 2013, for that year's third quarter report, Netflix reported its total of global streaming subscribers at 40.4 million (31.2 million in the United States).<sup id="cite_ref-NYT-8042332_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-8042332-52">[52]</a></sup> By the fourth quarter of 2013, Netflix reported 33.1 million United States subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> By September 2014, Netflix had subscribers in over 40 countries, with intentions of <a href="/wiki/International_expansion_of_Netflix" title="International expansion of Netflix">expanding their services in unreached countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> By October 2018, Netflix's customer base reached 137 million worldwide, confirming its rank as by far the world's biggest online subscription video service.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Netflix_Original_content">Early Netflix Original content</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early Netflix Original content" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Netflix has played a prominent role in <a href="/wiki/Independent_film" title="Independent film">independent film</a> distribution. Through its division <a href="/wiki/Red_Envelope_Entertainment" title="Red Envelope Entertainment">Red Envelope Entertainment</a>, Netflix licensed and distributed independent films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Born_into_Brothels" title="Born into Brothels">Born into Brothels</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Sherrybaby" title="Sherrybaby">Sherrybaby</a></i>. As of late 2006, <a href="/wiki/Red_Envelope_Entertainment" title="Red Envelope Entertainment">Red Envelope Entertainment</a> also expanded into producing original content with filmmakers such as <a href="/wiki/John_Waters" title="John Waters">John Waters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Netflix closed Red Envelope Entertainment in 2008, in part to avoid competition with its studio partners.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Entertainment_dominance.2C_presence.2C_and_continued_growth"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment_dominance,_presence,_and_continued_growth">Entertainment dominance, presence, and continued growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Entertainment dominance, presence, and continued growth" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Netflix has been one of the most successful <a href="/wiki/Dot-com_startup" class="mw-redirect" title="Dot-com startup">dot-com ventures</a>. In September 2002, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported that, at the time, Netflix mailed about 190,000 discs per day to its 670,000 monthly subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The company's published subscriber count increased from one million in the fourth quarter of 2002 to around 5.6 million at the end of the third quarter of 2006, to 14 million in March 2010. Netflix's early growth was fueled by the fast spread of <a href="/wiki/DVD_player" title="DVD player">DVD players</a> in households; in 2004, nearly two-thirds of United States homes had a DVD player. Netflix capitalized on the success of the DVD and its rapid expansion into United States homes, integrating the potential of the Internet and e-commerce to provide services and catalogs that bricks-and-mortar retailers could not compete with. Netflix also operates an online affiliate program which has helped to build online sales for DVD rentals as well. The company offers unlimited vacation time for salaried workers and allows employees to take any amount of their paychecks in stock options.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p><p>By 2010, Netflix's streaming business had grown so quickly that within months the company had shifted from the fastest-growing customer of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">United States Postal Service</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Mail" title="Mail">first-class service</a> to the largest source of Internet streaming traffic in North America in the evening. In November, it began offering a standalone streaming service separate from DVD rentals.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt20101125_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt20101125-61">[61]</a></sup> On September 18, 2011, Netflix announced its intentions to rebrand and restructure its DVD home media rental service as an independent subsidiary called Qwikster, separating DVD rental and streaming services.<sup id="cite_ref-QwiksterBlogPost_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QwiksterBlogPost-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Engadget-2011-09-19-Lawler_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Engadget-2011-09-19-Lawler-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Engadget-2011-09-19-Murph_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Engadget-2011-09-19-Murph-64">[64]</a></sup> Andy Rendich, a 12-year Netflix veteran, was to be CEO of Qwikster. Qwikster would carry video games whereas Netflix did not.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-65">[65]</a></sup> However, in October 2011, Netflix announced that it would retain its DVD service under the name Netflix and would not, in fact, create Qwikster for that purpose.<sup id="cite_ref-Engadget-6172362_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Engadget-6172362-66">[66]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2011, Netflix had over 23 million subscribers in the United States and over 26 million worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-netflix2011april_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-netflix2011april-67">[67]</a></sup> In July 2011, Netflix changed its prices, charging customers for its mail rental service and streaming service separately. This meant a price increase for customers who wanted to continue receiving both services.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> On October 24, Netflix announced 800,000 unsubscribers in the United States during the third quarter of 2011, and more losses were expected in the fourth quarter of 2011. However Netflix's income jumped 63% for the third quarter of 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Year-long, the total digital revenue for Netflix reached at least $1.5 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> On January 26, 2012, Netflix added 610,000 subscribers in the United States by the end of the fourth quarter of 2011, totaling 24.4 million United States subscribers for this time period.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> On October 23, however, Netflix announced an 88% decline in profits for the third quarter of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:324px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Netflixenvelope.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Netflixenvelope.jpg/322px-Netflixenvelope.jpg" decoding="async" width="322" height="197" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="490" data-file-height="300"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 322px;height: 197px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Netflixenvelope.jpg/322px-Netflixenvelope.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="322" data-height="197" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Netflixenvelope.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Opened Netflix rental envelope containing a DVD of <i><a href="/wiki/Coach_Carter" title="Coach Carter">Coach Carter</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>In April 2012, Netflix filed with the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Election_Commission" title="Federal Election Commission">Federal Election Commission</a> (FEC) to form a <a href="/wiki/Political_action_committee" title="Political action committee">political action committee</a> (PAC) called FLIXPAC.<sup id="cite_ref-FLIXPAC_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLIXPAC-74">[74]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Politico" title="Politico">Politico</a></i> referred to the PAC, based in <a href="/wiki/Los_Gatos,_California" title="Los Gatos, California">Los Gatos, California</a>, as "another political tool with which to aggressively press a pro-intellectual property, anti-video-piracy agenda".<sup id="cite_ref-FLIXPAC_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLIXPAC-74">[74]</a></sup> The hacktivist group <a href="/wiki/Anonymous_(group)" title="Anonymous (group)">Anonymous</a> called for a <a href="/wiki/Boycott" title="Boycott">boycott</a> of Netflix following the news.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Netflix spokesperson Joris Evers indicated that the PAC was not set up to support the <a href="/wiki/Stop_Online_Piracy_Act" title="Stop Online Piracy Act">Stop Online Piracy Act</a> (SOPA) and the <a href="/wiki/PROTECT_IP_Act" title="PROTECT IP Act">PROTECT IP Act</a> (PIPA), tweeting that the intent was to "engage on issues like <a href="/wiki/Network_neutrality" class="mw-redirect" title="Network neutrality">net neutrality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bandwidth_cap" class="mw-redirect" title="Bandwidth cap">bandwidth caps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Usage-based_billing" class="mw-redirect" title="Usage-based billing">UBB</a> and <a href="/wiki/Video_Privacy_Protection_Act" title="Video Privacy Protection Act">VPPA</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2013, Netflix announced it would be hosting its own awards ceremony, <i>The Flixies</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> On March 13, 2013, Netflix announced a Facebook implementation, letting United States subscribers access "Watched by your friends" and "Friends' Favorites" by agreeing.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> This was not legal until the <a href="/wiki/Video_Privacy_Protection_Act" title="Video Privacy Protection Act">Video Privacy Protection Act of 1988</a> was modified in early 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Rebranding_and_wider_international_expansion">Rebranding and wider international expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Rebranding and wider international expansion" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In April 2014, Netflix approached 50 million global subscribers with a 32.3% video streaming market share in the United States. Netflix operated in 41 countries around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters-2694084_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-2694084-81">[81]</a></sup> In June 2014, Netflix unveiled a global rebranding: a new logo, which uses a modern typeface with the <a href="/wiki/Drop_shadow" title="Drop shadow">drop shadowing</a> removed, and a new website <a href="/wiki/User_interface" title="User interface">UI</a>. The change was controversial; some liked the new minimalist design, whereas others felt more comfortable with the old interface.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> In July 2014, Netflix surpassed 50 million global subscribers, with 36 million of them being in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p><p>Following the launch of <i><a href="/wiki/Daredevil_(TV_series)" title="Daredevil (TV series)">Daredevil</a></i> in April 2015, Netflix director of content operations Tracy Wright announced that Netflix had added support for <a href="/wiki/Audio_description" title="Audio description">audio description</a> (a narration track that contains aural descriptions of key visual elements for the blind or visually impaired), and had begun to work with its partners to add descriptions to its other original series over time.<sup id="cite_ref-wp-blindsuperhero_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wp-blindsuperhero-84">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-variety-descriptions_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-variety-descriptions-85">[85]</a></sup> The following year, as part of a settlement with the <a href="/wiki/American_Council_of_the_Blind" title="American Council of the Blind">American Council of the Blind</a>, Netflix agreed to provide descriptions for its original series within 30 days of their premiere, and add <a href="/wiki/Screen_reader" title="Screen reader">screen reader</a> support and the ability to browse content by availability of descriptions.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p><p>At the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Electronics_Show" title="Consumer Electronics Show">Consumer Electronics Show</a>, Netflix announced a major international expansion of its service into 150 additional countries. Netflix promoted that with this expansion, it would now operate in nearly all countries that the company may legally or logistically operate in. A notable exception was China, citing the barriers of operating Internet and media services in the country due to its regulatory climate. Reed Hastings stated that the company was planning to build relationships with local media companies that could serve as partners for distributing its content in the country (with a goal to concentrate primarily on its original content), but stated that they were in no hurry, and could thus take "many years".<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thr-iquyideal_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thr-iquyideal-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vb-130new_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vb-130new-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-engadget-nearlyevery_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-engadget-nearlyevery-90">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-verge-netflixeverywhere_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-netflixeverywhere-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-recode-netflixnearly_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recode-netflixnearly-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnet-nearlyevery_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnet-nearlyevery-93">[93]</a></sup></p><p>Also in January 2016, Netflix announced it would begin <a href="/wiki/VPN_blocking" title="VPN blocking">blocking</a> <a href="/wiki/Virtual_private_network" title="Virtual private network">virtual private networks</a>, or VPNs.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> At the same time, Netflix reported 74.8 million subscribers and predicted it would add 6.1 million more by March 2016. Subscription growth has been fueled by its global expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> By the end of the year, Netflix added a feature to allow customers to download and play select movies and shows while offline.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2017, Netflix signed a <a href="/wiki/Music_publisher_(popular_music)" title="Music publisher (popular music)">music publishing</a> deal with <a href="/wiki/BMG_Rights_Management" title="BMG Rights Management">BMG Rights Management</a>, where BMG will oversee rights outside of the United States for music associated with Netflix original content. Netflix continues to handle these tasks in-house in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> On April 17, 2017, it was reported that Netflix was nearing 100 million subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-subscribers_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-subscribers-98">[98]</a></sup> On April 25, 2017, Netflix announced that it had reached a licensing deal in China with the <a href="/wiki/Baidu" title="Baidu">Baidu</a>-owned streaming service <a href="/wiki/IQiyi" title="IQiyi">iQiyi</a>, to allow selected Netflix original content to be distributed in China on the platform.<sup id="cite_ref-thr-iquyideal_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thr-iquyideal-88">[88]</a></sup>
The <i>Los Angeles Times</i> stated: "Its series and movies account for more than a third of all prime-time download Internet traffic in North America."<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p><p>On August 7, 2017, Netflix acquired <a href="/wiki/Millarworld" title="Millarworld">Millarworld</a>, the creator-owned publishing company of comic book writer <a href="/wiki/Mark_Millar" title="Mark Millar">Mark Millar</a>. It is the first ever company acquisition in Netflix's history. Netflix plans to leverage Millar and his current and future work for future original content. Chief content officer Ted Sarandos described Millar as being a "modern-day <a href="/wiki/Stan_Lee" title="Stan Lee">Stan Lee</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> The following week, Netflix announced that it had entered into an exclusive development deal with <a href="/wiki/Shonda_Rhimes" title="Shonda Rhimes">Shonda Rhimes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-rhimesnetflix_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-rhimesnetflix-101">[101]</a></sup></p><p>On January 22, 2018, the company crossed $100 billion in market capitalization, becoming the largest digital media and entertainment company in the world, bigger than every traditional media company except for <a href="/wiki/AT%26T" title="AT&amp;T">AT&amp;T</a>, <a href="/wiki/Comcast" title="Comcast">Comcast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disney" class="mw-redirect" title="Disney">Disney</a><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> and the 59th largest publicly traded company in the US S&amp;P 500 Index.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p><p>On March 2, 2018, Netflix stock price surged to a new all-time high of $301.05 beating its 12-month price target of $300.00, and finishing the session with a market capitalization of $130 billion putting it within shouting distance of traditional media giants like Disney ($155 billion) and Comcast ($169 billion). The milestone came a day after British satcaster Sky announced a new agreement with Netflix to integrate Netflix's subscription VOD offering into its pay-TV service. Customers with its high-end Sky Q set-top box and service will be able to see Netflix titles alongside their regular Sky channels.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p><p>On August 16, 2018, Netflix announced a three-year overall deal with <i><a href="/wiki/Black-ish" title="Black-ish">black-ish</a></i> creator <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Barris" title="Kenya Barris">Kenya Barris</a>. Under the deal, Barris will produce new series exclusively at Netflix, writing and executive producing all projects through his production company, Khalabo Ink Society.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p><p>On August 27, 2018, Netflix signed a five-year exclusive overall deal with international best–selling author <a href="/wiki/Harlan_Coben" title="Harlan Coben">Harlan Coben</a>. Under the multi-million pact, Netflix will work with Coben to develop 14 existing titles and future projects.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> On the same day, the company inked an overall deal with <i><a href="/wiki/Gravity_Falls" title="Gravity Falls">Gravity Falls</a></i> creator <a href="/wiki/Alex_Hirsch" title="Alex Hirsch">Alex Hirsch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p><p>According to Global Internet Phenomena Report Netflix consumes 15% of all Internet bandwidth globally, the most by any single application.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2018, Netflix acquired ABQ Studios, a film and TV production facility with eight sound stages in Albuquerque, New Mexico. The reported purchase price is under $30 million.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p><p>In November 2018, <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">Paramount Pictures</a> signed a multi-picture film deal with Netflix as part of <a href="/wiki/Viacom_(2005%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Viacom (2005–present)">Viacom</a>'s growth strategy, making Paramount the first major film studio to sign a deal with Netflix.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> A sequel to <a href="/wiki/AwesomenessTV" title="AwesomenessTV">Awesomeness Films</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/To_All_the_Boys_I%27ve_Loved_Before_(film)" title="To All the Boys I've Loved Before (film)">To All the Boys I've Loved Before</a></i> is currently in development at the studio for Netflix.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p><p>Netflix sought and was approved for membership into the <a href="/wiki/Motion_Picture_Association_of_America" title="Motion Picture Association of America">Motion Picture Association of America</a> (MPAA) on January 22, 2019, as the first streaming service to become a member of the association.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2019, Netflix acquired the <a href="/wiki/StoryBots" title="StoryBots">StoryBots</a> children's media franchise as part of a commitment to expand its educational content.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p><p>On May 9, 2019, Netflix made a deal with <a href="/wiki/Dark_Horse_Entertainment" title="Dark Horse Entertainment">Dark Horse Entertainment</a> to make television series and films based on comics from <a href="/wiki/Dark_Horse_Comics" title="Dark Horse Comics">Dark Horse Comics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p><p>In early August 2019, Netflix negotiated an exclusive multi-year film and television deal with <i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones" title="Game of Thrones">Game of Thrones</a></i> showrunners <a href="/wiki/David_Benioff" title="David Benioff">David Benioff</a> and <a href="/wiki/D.B._Weiss" class="mw-redirect" title="D.B. Weiss">D.B. Weiss</a> reportedly worth US$200 million.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> As a result of their commitments to Netflix, Benioff and Weiss withdrew from an earlier agreement with Disney to write and produce a <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a> film series.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p><p>On November 13, 2019, Netflix and <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon" title="Nickelodeon">Nickelodeon</a> entered into a multiyear content production agreement to produce several original animated feature films and television series based on Nickelodeon's library of characters, in order to compete with <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">Disney</a>'s new streaming service <a href="/wiki/Disney%2B" title="Disney+">Disney+</a>, which had launched the day before. This agreement expanded on their existing relationship, in which new specials based on the past Nickelodeon series <i><a href="/wiki/Invader_Zim" title="Invader Zim">Invader Zim</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Rocko%27s_Modern_Life" title="Rocko's Modern Life">Rocko's Modern Life</a></i> were released by Netflix. New projects planned under the team-up include a music project featuring <a href="/wiki/Squidward_Tentacles" title="Squidward Tentacles">Squidward Tentacles</a> from the animated television series <i><a href="/wiki/SpongeBob_SquarePants" title="SpongeBob SquarePants">SpongeBob SquarePants</a></i>, and films based on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Loud_House" title="The Loud House">The Loud House</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Rise_of_the_Teenage_Mutant_Ninja_Turtles" title="Rise of the Teenage Mutant Ninja Turtles">Rise of the Teenage Mutant Ninja Turtles</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p><p>On February 25, 2020, Netflix formed partnerships with six Japanese creators to produce an original Japanese anime project. This partnership include manga creator group CLAMP, mangaka Shin Kibayashi, mangaka Yasuo Ohtagaki, novelist and film director Otsuichi, novelist Tow Ubutaka, and manga creator Mari Yamazaki.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Ownership" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<p>As of 2017, Netflix shares were mainly held by institutional investors, including <a href="/wiki/Capital_Group_Companies" title="Capital Group Companies">Capital Group Companies</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Vanguard_Group" title="The Vanguard Group">The Vanguard Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/BlackRock" title="BlackRock">BlackRock</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance">Finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Finance" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>For the fiscal year 2018, Netflix reported earnings of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>1.21 billion, with an annual revenue of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>15.8 billion, an increase of approximately 116% over the previous fiscal cycle. Netflix's shares traded at over $400 per share at its highest price in 2018, and its market capitalization reached a value of over <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>180 billion in June 2018. Netflix ranked 261 on the 2018 <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a></i> list of the largest United States companies by revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Netflix was announced to be the number one best <a href="/wiki/Stock" title="Stock">stock</a> in the 2010s, with a total return of 3,693%.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
