<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Video games" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In June 2018, Netflix announced a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Telltale_Games" title="Telltale Games">Telltale Games</a> to port its <a href="/wiki/Adventure_game" title="Adventure game">adventure games</a> to the service in a streaming video format. The games would be adapted to be similar to the existing interactive narrative stories that Netflix already offers, allowing simple controls through a television remote. The first such game, <i><a href="/wiki/Minecraft:_Story_Mode" title="Minecraft: Story Mode">Minecraft: Story Mode</a></i>, was expected to be released later in the year, and Telltale also received rights to produce a video game adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/Stranger_Things" title="Stranger Things">Stranger Things</a></i> for conventional gaming platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup> In September 2018, Telltale underwent a "majority studio closure" and laid off nearly its entire staff beyond a skeleton crew of 25 employees, citing a loss of funding. Netflix stated that while the <i>Minecraft: Story Mode</i> port would go on, the company was seeking alternate options for the <i>Stranger Things</i> project.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Device_support_and_technical_details">Device support and technical details</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Device support and technical details" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Netflix-compatible_devices" title="List of Netflix-compatible devices">List of Netflix-compatible devices</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Technical_details_of_Netflix" title="Technical details of Netflix">Technical details of Netflix</a></div>
<p>Netflix can be accessed via an <a href="/wiki/Internet_browser" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet browser">internet browser</a> on PCs, while Netflix apps are available on various platforms, including <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" class="mw-redirect" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray Disc</a> players, <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablet computers</a>, mobile phones, <a href="/wiki/Smart_TV" title="Smart TV">smart TVs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Digital_media_player" title="Digital media player">digital media players</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Video_game_console" title="Video game console">video game consoles</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Xbox_One" title="Xbox One">Xbox One</a>, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wii_U" title="Wii U">Wii U</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a> and the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a> were formerly compatible with Netflix as well.
</p><p>In addition, a growing number of <a href="/wiki/Multichannel_television" title="Multichannel television">multichannel television</a> providers, including cable television and <a href="/wiki/IPTV" class="mw-redirect" title="IPTV">IPTV</a> services, have also added Netflix apps accessible within their own <a href="/wiki/Set-top_box" title="Set-top box">set-top boxes</a>, sometimes with the ability for its content (along with those of other online video services) to be presented within a unified search interface alongside linear television programming as an "all-in-one" solution.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup></p><p>4K streaming requires a 4K-compatible device and display, both supporting <a href="/wiki/HDCP" class="mw-redirect" title="HDCP">HDCP</a> 2.2. 4K streaming on personal computers requires hardware and software support of the Microsoft <a href="/wiki/PlayReady" title="PlayReady">PlayReady</a> 3.0 <a href="/wiki/Digital_rights_management" title="Digital rights management">digital rights management</a> solution, which requires a compatible CPU, graphics card, and software environment. Currently, this feature is limited to <a href="/wiki/Kaby_Lake" title="Kaby Lake">7th generation</a> <a href="/wiki/Intel_Core" title="Intel Core">Intel Core</a> or later CPUs, <a href="/wiki/Windows_10" title="Windows 10">Windows 10</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nvidia" title="Nvidia">Nvidia</a> <a href="/wiki/Geforce_10_series" class="mw-redirect" title="Geforce 10 series">Geforce 10 series</a> and AMD <a href="/wiki/AMD_Radeon_400_series" class="mw-redirect" title="AMD Radeon 400 series">Radeon 400 series</a> or later graphics cards, and running through <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Edge" title="Microsoft Edge">Microsoft Edge</a> web browser, or the Netflix <a href="/wiki/Universal_app" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal app">universal app</a> available on <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Store_(digital)" title="Microsoft Store (digital)">Microsoft Store</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pcw-playready4k_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcw-playready4k-273">[273]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-techradar-4k_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techradar-4k-274">[274]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ars-netflix4k_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-netflix4k-275">[275]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nvidia_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nvidia-276">[276]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AMD_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMD-277">[277]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Sales_and_marketing">Sales and marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sales and marketing" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Netflix_booth_(36079051696).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Netflix_booth_%2836079051696%29.jpg/220px-Netflix_booth_%2836079051696%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="3840"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Netflix_booth_%2836079051696%29.jpg/220px-Netflix_booth_%2836079051696%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Netflix_booth_(36079051696).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Netflix's booth at the 2017 <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con" title="San Diego Comic-Con">San Diego Comic-Con</a></div></div></div>
<p>During Q1 2011, sales and rentals of DVDs and Blu-ray discs plunged about 35%, and the sell-through of packaged discs fell 19.99% to $2.07 billion, with more money spent on subscription than in-store rentals. This decrease was attributed to the rising popularity of Netflix and other streaming services.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2012, Netflix hired Kelly Bennett – former Warner Bros. Vice President of Interactive, Worldwide Marketing – to become its new chief marketing officer. This also filled a vacancy at Netflix that had been empty for over six months when their previous CMO Leslie Kilgore left in January 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup></p><p>Netflix's website has 117.6 million subscribers as of 2018, with 8.3 million being added in the fourth quarter of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup> As of January 28, 2018, Netflix's website ranked as the 30th most trafficked website in the world and 9th most trafficked website in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup></p><p>Netflix has a Twitter feed, used to tweet about the new and upcoming shows that include <a href="/wiki/Hashtags" class="mw-redirect" title="Hashtags">hashtags</a> to encourage engagement of their audience to not only watch the show but to contribute to the hashtag themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="International_expansion">International expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: International expansion" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_expansion_of_Netflix" title="International expansion of Netflix">International expansion of Netflix</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Netflix_area.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Netflix_area.svg/300px-Netflix_area.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="154" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="863" data-file-height="443"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 300px;height: 154px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Netflix_area.svg/300px-Netflix_area.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="300" data-height="154" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Netflix_area.svg/450px-Netflix_area.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Netflix_area.svg/600px-Netflix_area.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Netflix_area.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Availability of Netflix, as of January 2016:<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #B00000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Available</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Not available</div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Netflix_at_Thong_Lor.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Netflix_at_Thong_Lor.jpg/220px-Netflix_at_Thong_Lor.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2976" data-file-height="3968"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 293px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Netflix_at_Thong_Lor.jpg/220px-Netflix_at_Thong_Lor.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="293" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Netflix_at_Thong_Lor.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Netflix advertising at <a href="/wiki/Thong_Lo_BTS_station" title="Thong Lo BTS station">Thong Lo BTS station</a>, Bangkok</div></div></div>
<table class="wikitable"><tbody><tr><th>2007
</th>
<td>Netflix began streaming in the United States.
</td></tr><tr><th>2010
</th>
<td>The company first began offering streaming service to the international market on September 22, 2010, in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-Canada_Stumble_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canada_Stumble-283">[283]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th>2011
</th>
<td>Netflix expanded its streaming service to Latin America, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Guianas" class="mw-redirect" title="Guianas">Guianas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LA_Expansion_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Expansion-284">[284]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th>2012
</th>
<td>Netflix started its expansion to Europe in 2012, launching in the United Kingdom and Ireland on January 4.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-285">[285]</a></sup> By October 18 it had expanded to <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-prnewswire.com_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prnewswire.com-286">[286]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th>2013
</th>
<td>The company decided to slow expansion to control subscription costs.<sup id="cite_ref-6_March_2014_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6_March_2014-287">[287]</a></sup> It only expanded to the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>.
</td></tr><tr><th>2014
</th>
<td>Netflix became available in <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Netflix_Media_Centre_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Netflix_Media_Centre-288">[288]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th>2015
</th>
<td>Netflix expanded to Australia and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, Japan,<sup id="cite_ref-Netflix_Aus_and_NZ_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Netflix_Aus_and_NZ-289">[289]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Netflix_Japan_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Netflix_Japan-291">[291]</a></sup> Italy, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, and Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th>2016
</th>
<td>Netflix announced at the <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Electronics_Show" title="Consumer Electronics Show">Consumer Electronics Show</a> in January 2016 that it had become available worldwide except <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> and the territory of <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th>2017
</th>
<td>In April 2017, Netflix confirmed it had reached a licensing deal in China for original Netflix content with <a href="/wiki/IQiyi" title="IQiyi">IQiyi</a>, a Chinese video streaming platform owned by <a href="/wiki/Baidu" title="Baidu">Baidu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><p>As of October 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Netflix officially supports 26 languages for <a href="/wiki/User_interface" title="User interface">user interface</a> and <a href="/wiki/Customer_support" title="Customer support">customer support</a> purposes: Arabic (<a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Modern Standard</a>), Chinese (<a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">Simplified</a> and <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">Traditional</a>), Czech, Danish, Dutch, English, Finnish, French, German, Greek, Hebrew, Hungarian, Indonesian, Italian, Japanese, Korean, Norwegian (<a href="/wiki/Bokm%C3%A5l" title="Bokmål">Bokmål</a>), Polish, Portuguese (<a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Portuguese" title="Brazilian Portuguese">Brazilian</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Portuguese" title="European Portuguese">European</a>), Romanian, Spanish (<a href="/wiki/Castilian_Spanish" title="Castilian Spanish">Castilian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_Americas" title="Spanish language in the Americas">Latin American</a>), Swahili, Swedish, Thai, Turkish and Vietnamese.<sup id="cite_ref-Netflix_Language_Preferences_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Netflix_Language_Preferences-296">[296]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup></p><p>Netflix has encountered political controversy after its global expansion and for some of its international productions, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mechanism_(TV_series)" title="The Mechanism (TV series)">The Mechanism</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Fauda" title="Fauda">Fauda</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Amo_(TV_series)" title="Amo (TV series)">Amo</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup> In June 2016, Russian Minister of Culture <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Medinsky" title="Vladimir Medinsky">Vladimir Medinsky</a> asserted that Netflix is part of a US government plot to influence the world culture, "to enter every home, get into every television, and through that television, into the head of every person on earth". This was part of his argument for the increase of funding of Russian cinema to pitch it against the dominance of Hollywood.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2020 the company released its first report of when it has complied with government requested content takedowns in their countries, a total of 9 times since its launch:<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li>In Singapore, Netflix complied with requests to take down <i><a href="/wiki/Cooking_on_High" title="Cooking on High">Cooking on High</a></i>, <i>The Legend of 420</i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Disjointed" title="Disjointed">Disjointed</a></i> in 2018, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Temptation_of_Christ_(film)" title="The Last Temptation of Christ (film)">The Last Temptation of Christ</a></i> in 2019, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Hangover" title="The Last Hangover">The Last Hangover</a></i> in 2020.</li>
<li>In Germany,  Netflix complied with a request to take down a version of <i>Night of the Living Dead</i> in 2017.</li>
<li>In Vietnam,  Netflix complied with a request to take down <i><a href="/wiki/Full_Metal_Jacket" title="Full Metal Jacket">Full Metal Jacket</a></i> in 2017.</li>
<li>In New Zealand, Netflix complied with a request to take down the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bridge_(2006_documentary_film)" title="The Bridge (2006 documentary film)">The Bridge</a></i> in 2015. The film is deemed objectionable by the country's <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Film_and_Literature_Classification_(New_Zealand)" title="Office of Film and Literature Classification (New Zealand)">Office of Film and Literature Classification</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup></li>
<li>In Saudi Arabia, Netflix complied with a request to take down an episode criticizing the country's government from the series <i><a href="/wiki/Patriot_Act_with_Hasan_Minhaj" title="Patriot Act with Hasan Minhaj">Patriot Act with Hasan Minhaj</a></i> in 2019, which drew criticism in the media.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup></li></ul><p>In India, Netflix along with its local competitor Hotstar announced plans in early 2019 to adopt self-regulation guidelines for content streamed on their platforms within the country in an effort to prevent potential implementation of government censorship laws.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup> The Jordanian series <i><a href="/wiki/Jinn_(TV_series)" title="Jinn (TV series)">Jinn</a></i> was condemned by members of the country's government for contravening the country's moral standards, and the country's highest prosecutor has sought to have the series banned from streaming.<sup id="cite_ref-io9Jinn_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-io9Jinn-308">[308]</a></sup> On September 3, 2019, Netflix applied for a license to continue its streaming services in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, under the country's new broadcasting rules. The television watchdog of <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radio_and_Television_Supreme_Council" title="Radio and Television Supreme Council">Radio and Television Supreme Council</a> (RTÜK) issued new guidelines, under which content providers were required to get new license for operating in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Worldwide_users">Worldwide users</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Worldwide users" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>

</td></tr></tbody></table></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Competitors">Competitors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Competitors" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Online_DVD_rental" class="mw-redirect" title="Online DVD rental">Online DVD rental</a> and <a href="/wiki/Video_on_demand" title="Video on demand">Video on demand</a></div>
<p>Netflix's success was followed by the establishment of numerous other DVD rental companies, both in the United States and abroad. <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a> began an online rental service in October 2002 but left the market in May 2005. However, Walmart later acquired the rental service <a href="/wiki/Vudu" title="Vudu">Vudu</a> in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Blockbuster_Video" class="mw-redirect" title="Blockbuster Video">Blockbuster Video</a> entered the United States online market in August 2004, with a US$19.95 monthly subscription service (equivalent to $27 in 2019). This sparked a <a href="/wiki/Price_war" title="Price war">price war</a>; Netflix had raised its popular three-disc plan from US$19.95 to US$21.99 just prior to Blockbuster's launch, but by October, Netflix reduced this fee to US$17.99. Blockbuster responded with rates as low as US$14.99 for a time, but, by August 2005, both companies settled at identical rates.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">[315]</a></sup> On July 22, 2007, Netflix dropped the prices of its two most popular plans by US$1.00 in an effort to better compete with Blockbuster's online-only offerings.<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup> On October 4, 2012, <a href="/wiki/Dish_Network" title="Dish Network">Dish Network</a> scrapped plans to make Blockbuster into a Netflix competitor.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup> (Dish bought the ailing Blockbuster, LLC in 2011 and will continue to license the brand name to franchise locations, and keep its "Blockbuster on Demand" video streaming service open.)<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup></p><p>In 2005, Netflix cited Amazon.com as a potential competitor,<sup id="cite_ref-C4WDefault-5450355_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C4WDefault-5450355-319">[319]</a></sup> which until 2008, offered online video rentals in the United Kingdom and Germany. This arm of the business was eventually sold to LoveFilm; however, Amazon then bought LoveFilm in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup> In addition, Amazon now streams movies and television shows through Amazon Video (formerly Amazon Video On Demand and LOVEFiLM Instant).<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Redbox" title="Redbox">Redbox</a> is another competitor that uses a <a href="/wiki/Kiosk" title="Kiosk">kiosk</a> approach: Rather than mailing DVDs, customers pick up and return DVDs at self-service kiosks located in metropolitan areas. In September 2012, <a href="/wiki/Coinstar" title="Coinstar">Coinstar</a>, the owners of Redbox, announced plans to partner with <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Communications" title="Verizon Communications">Verizon</a> to launch <i>Redbox Instant by Verizon</i> by late 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup> In early 2013, <i>Redbox Instant by Verizon</i> began a limited beta release of its service,<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">[323]</a></sup> which was described by critics as "No Netflix killer"<sup id="cite_ref-CNET_324-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNET-324">[324]</a></sup> due to "glitches [and] lackluster selection".<sup id="cite_ref-NASDAQ_325-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASDAQ-325">[325]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/CuriosityStream" title="CuriosityStream">CuriosityStream</a>, a premium ad-free, subscription-based service launched in March 2015 similar to Netflix but offering strictly nonfiction content in the areas of science, technology, civilization and the human spirit, has been dubbed the "new Netflix for non-fiction".<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Hulu_Plus" class="mw-redirect" title="Hulu Plus">Hulu Plus</a>, like Netflix and Amazon Prime Instant Video, "ink[s] their own deals for exclusive and original content", requiring Netflix "not only to continue to attract new subscribers, but also keep existing ones happy".<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">[327]</a></sup></p><p>Netflix largely avoids offering pornography, but several "adult video" subscription services were inspired by Netflix, such as <a href="/wiki/SugarInstant" title="SugarInstant">SugarInstant</a> and <a href="/wiki/WantedList" title="WantedList">WantedList</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">[328]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">[329]</a></sup></p><p>In Australia, Netflix most notably competes with <a href="/wiki/Stan_(company)" title="Stan (company)">Stan</a>, the local SVOD competitor that only operates in the Australian marketplace and currently undercuts Netflix on monthly pricing while using extensive original Australian content as its major value proposition. Netflix currently holds a sizeable lead in market share over Stan, with Netflix reaching over 11.5 million household users in Australia in 2019 compared to Stan reaching over 2.5 million household users in the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">[330]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">[331]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic countries</a>, Netflix competes with <a href="/wiki/Viaplay" class="mw-redirect" title="Viaplay">Viaplay</a>, <a href="/wiki/HBO_Nordic" class="mw-redirect" title="HBO Nordic">HBO Nordic</a> and <a href="/wiki/C_More" class="mw-redirect" title="C More">C More</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">[332]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">[333]</a></sup> In Southeast Asia, Netflix competes with <a href="/wiki/HOOQ" title="HOOQ">HOOQ</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">[334]</a></sup> Astro On the Go, Sky on Demand, <a href="/wiki/Singtel_TV" title="Singtel TV">Singtel TV</a>, HomeCable OnDemand, and <a href="/wiki/Iflix" title="Iflix">iflix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">[335]</a></sup> In New Zealand, Netflix competes with local streaming companies including <a href="/wiki/Television_New_Zealand" class="mw-redirect" title="Television New Zealand">Television New Zealand</a> (TVNZ),<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">[336]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mediaworks_New_Zealand" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediaworks New Zealand">Mediaworks New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sky_Network_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Sky Network Television">Sky Network Television</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">[337]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lightbox_(New_Zealand)" title="Lightbox (New Zealand)">Lightbox</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">[338]</a></sup> Neon and <a href="/wiki/Quickflix" title="Quickflix">Quickflix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">[339]</a></sup> In Italy, Netflix competes with Infinity, <a href="/wiki/Now_TV_(Sky_plc)" class="mw-redirect" title="Now TV (Sky plc)">Now TV</a> and TIMvision.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">[340]</a></sup> In South Africa, Netflix competes with <a href="/wiki/Showmax" title="Showmax">Showmax</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">[341]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/MENA" title="MENA">MENA</a> region, Netflix competes with <a href="/wiki/Icflix" title="Icflix">icflix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starz" title="Starz">Starz Play Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/OSN" title="OSN">OSN</a>'s Wavo, and <a href="/wiki/Iflix" title="Iflix">iflix Arabia</a>. Also, in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, Netflix competes with <a href="/wiki/Rede_Globo" title="Rede Globo">Globoplay</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Grupo_Globo" title="Grupo Globo">Grupo Globo</a>'s streaming service, and <a href="/wiki/RecordTV" title="RecordTV">PlayPlus</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Grupo_Record" title="Grupo Record">Grupo Record</a>'s streaming service.
</p><p>In Mexico, <a href="/wiki/Televisa" title="Televisa">Televisa</a> removed its content from Netflix in 2016 and moved it to its own streaming service <a href="/wiki/Blim" class="mw-redirect" title="Blim">Blim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">[342]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a> launched their own streaming service, <a href="/wiki/Disney%2B" title="Disney+">Disney+</a>, in November 2019. As a result, Disney content currently hosted on Netflix will begin to be phased out over the next couple of years.<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">[343]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">[344]</a></sup> Disney reported in early 2020 that their subscriber count had blown past internal and industry estimates at 50 million globally - a 22 million increase since the prior report two months earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">[345]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(11)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents">Incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Incidents" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-11 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-11">
<p>In February 2019, police stormed the Netflix headquarters in Hollywood after a man with a gun was reported wandering around the premises. The buildings were placed on lockdown.<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">[346]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(12)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Awards" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-12 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-12">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_Netflix" title="List of accolades received by Netflix">List of accolades received by Netflix</a></div>
<p>On July 18, 2013, Netflix earned the first <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award" title="Primetime Emmy Award">Primetime Emmy Award</a> nominations for original online-only <a href="/wiki/Web_television" title="Web television">web television</a> programs at the <a href="/wiki/65th_Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="65th Primetime Emmy Awards">65th Primetime Emmy Awards</a>. Three of its web series, <i>Arrested Development</i>, <i>Hemlock Grove</i> and <i>House of Cards</i>, earned a combined 14 nominations (nine for <i>House of Cards</i>, three for <i>Arrested Development</i> and two for <i>Hemlock Grove</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-NDWi2PEN_347-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NDWi2PEN-347">[347]</a></sup> The <i>House of Cards</i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Chapter_1_(House_of_Cards)" title="Chapter 1 (House of Cards)">Chapter 1</a>" received four nominations for both the 65th Primetime Emmy Awards and <a href="/wiki/65th_Primetime_Creative_Arts_Emmy_Awards" title="65th Primetime Creative Arts Emmy Awards">65th Primetime Creative Arts Emmy Awards</a>, becoming the first <a href="/wiki/Webisode" title="Webisode">webisode</a> of a television series to receive a major Primetime Emmy Award nomination: David Fincher was nominated in the category of Outstanding Directing for a Drama Series.<sup id="cite_ref-NDWi2PEN_347-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NDWi2PEN-347">[347]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">[348]</a></sup> "Chapter 1" joined <i>Arrested Development</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> "<a href="/wiki/Flight_of_the_Phoenix_(Arrested_Development)" title="Flight of the Phoenix (Arrested Development)">Flight of the Phoenix</a>" and <i>Hemlock Grove</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> "Children of the Night" as the first webisodes to earn Creative Arts Emmy Award nomination, and with its win for Outstanding Cinematography for a Single-Camera Series, "Chapter 1" became the first webisode to be awarded an Emmy.<sup id="cite_ref-NMHWTPCAEA_349-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NMHWTPCAEA-349">[349]</a></sup> Fincher's win for Directing for a Drama Series made the episode the first Primetime Emmy-awarded webisode.<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">[350]</a></sup></p><p>On December 12, 2013, the network earned six <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Awards" title="Golden Globe Awards">Golden Globe Award</a> nominations, including four for <i>House of Cards</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">[351]</a></sup> Among those nominations was Wright for <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actress_%E2%80%93_Television_Series_Drama" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actress – Television Series Drama">Golden Globe Award for Best Actress – Television Series Drama</a> for her portrayal of Claire Underwood, which she won at the <a href="/wiki/71st_Golden_Globe_Awards" title="71st Golden Globe Awards">71st Golden Globe Awards</a> on January 12. With the accolade, Wright became the first actress to win a Golden Globe for an online-only web television series. It also marked Netflix' first major acting award.<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">[352]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">[353]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">[354]</a></sup> <i>House of Cards</i> and <i>Orange is the New Black</i> also won <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Peabody Awards">Peabody Awards</a> in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">[355]</a></sup></p><p>On July 10, 2014, Netflix received 31 Emmy nominations. Among other nominations, <i>House of Cards</i> received nominations for Outstanding Drama Series, Outstanding Directing in a Drama Series and Outstanding Writing in a Drama Series. Kevin Spacey and Robin Wright were nominated for Outstanding Lead Actor and Outstanding Lead Actress in a Drama Series. <i>Orange is the New Black</i> was nominated in the comedy categories, earning nominations for Outstanding Comedy Series, Outstanding Writing for a Comedy Series and Outstanding Directing for a Comedy Series. Taylor Schilling, Kate Mulgrew and Uzo Aduba were respectively nominated for Outstanding Lead Actress in a Comedy Series, Outstanding Supporting Actress in a Comedy Series and Outstanding Guest Actress in a Comedy Series (the latter was for Aduba's recurring role in season one, as she was promoted to series regular for the show's second season).<sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">[356]</a></sup></p><p>Netflix got the largest share of 2016 Emmy award nominations among its competitors, with 16 major nominations. However, streaming shows only got 24 nominations out of a total of 139, falling significantly behind cable.<sup id="cite_ref-digitaljournal.com_357-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-digitaljournal.com-357">[357]</a></sup> The 16 Netflix nominees were: <i>House of Cards</i> with Kevin Spacey, <i>A Very Murray Christmas</i> with Bill Murray, <i>Unbreakable Kimmy Schmidt</i>, <i>Master of None</i>, and <i>Bloodline</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-digitaljournal.com_357-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-digitaljournal.com-357">[357]</a></sup></p><p><i>Stranger Things</i> received 19 nominations at the <a href="/wiki/69th_Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="69th Primetime Emmy Awards">2017 Primetime Emmy Awards</a>, while <i><a href="/wiki/The_Crown_(TV_series)" title="The Crown (TV series)">The Crown</a></i> received 13 nominations.<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">[358]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2017, Netflix was nominated for Broadcaster of the Year in the UK's Diversity in Media Awards.
</p><p>In December 2017, Netflix was awarded <a href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals" title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals">PETA</a>'s Company of the Year for promoting animal rights movies and documentaries like <i><a href="/wiki/Forks_Over_Knives" title="Forks Over Knives">Forks Over Knives</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/What_the_Health" title="What the Health">What the Health</a></i>.
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/90th_Academy_Awards" title="90th Academy Awards">90th Academy Awards</a>, held on March 4, 2018, Netflix won the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Documentary_Feature" title="Academy Award for Best Documentary Feature">Oscar for Best Documentary Feature</a> for the film <i><a href="/wiki/Icarus_(2017_film)" title="Icarus (2017 film)">Icarus</a>.</i> During his remarks backstage, director and writer Bryan Fogel remarked that Netflix had "single-handedly changed the documentary world". <i>Icarus</i> had its premiere at the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Sundance_Film_Festival" title="Sundance Film Festival">Sundance Film Festival</a> and was bought by Netflix for $5 million, one of the biggest deals ever for a non-fiction film.<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">[359]</a></sup></p><p>Netflix became the most nominated network at the 2018 <a href="/wiki/70th_Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="70th Primetime Emmy Awards">Primetime</a> and <a href="/wiki/70th_Primetime_Creative_Arts_Emmy_Awards" title="70th Primetime Creative Arts Emmy Awards">Creative Arts Emmy Awards</a> with 112 nominations, therefore breaking <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a>'s 17-years record as most nominated network at the Emmys, who received 108 nominations.<sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">[360]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">[361]</a></sup></p><p>On January 22, 2019, Netflix scored 15 nominations for the <a href="/wiki/91st_Academy_Awards" title="91st Academy Awards">91st Academy Awards</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture" title="Academy Award for Best Picture">Best Picture</a> for <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Cuar%C3%B3n" title="Alfonso Cuarón">Alfonso Cuarón</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Roma_(2018_film)" title="Roma (2018 film)">Roma</a></i>, which was nominated for 10 awards.<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">[362]</a></sup> The 15 nominations equal the total nominations Netflix had received in previous years. Its increased presence in the Academy Awards has led filmmakers such as <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a> to speak out against the nomination of streaming content. As a possible solution, Netflix is in the process of buying <a href="/wiki/Grauman%27s_Egyptian_Theatre" title="Grauman's Egyptian Theatre">Grauman's Egyptian Theatre</a> to host events and screen its films and series.<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">[363]</a></sup> However, there are no plans to roll out full theatrical releases there.<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">[364]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(13)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance_and_revenue">Finance and revenue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Finance and revenue" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-13 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-13">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2010">2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: 2010" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2010, Netflix's stock price increased 219% to $175.70 and it added eight million subscribers, bringing its total to 20 million. Revenue jumped 29% to $2.16 billion and net income was up 39% to $161 million.<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">[365]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2011">2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: 2011" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In April 2011, Netflix was expected to earn $1.07 a share in the first quarter of 2011 on revenue of $705.7 million, a huge increase compared to the year-earlier profit of 59¢ on revenue of $493.7 million, according to a survey of 25 analysts polled by FactSet Research.<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">[366]</a></sup></p><p>At their peak, in July 2011, Netflix shares were trading for $299. Following the customer dissatisfaction and resulting loss of subscribers after the announcements by CEO Hastings that streaming and DVD rental would be charged separately, leading to a higher price for customers who wanted both (on September 1), and that the DVD rental would be split off as the subsidiary Qwikster (on September 18), the share price fell steeply, to around $130.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">[367]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">[368]</a></sup> However, on October 10, 2011, plans to split the company were scrapped. The reason being that "two websites would make things more difficult", he stated on the Netflix blog. On November 22, Netflix's share tumbled, as share prices fell by as much as 7%.<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">[369]</a></sup> By December 2011, as a consequence of its decision to raise prices, Netflix had lost over 75% of its total value from the summer.<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">[370]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">[371]</a></sup> Describing their business model as "broken", Wedbush downgraded Netflix's stock rating to "underperform", the equivalent of sell.<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">[372]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2014">2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: 2014" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In May 2014, Netflix increased the fee for UK subscribers by £1.<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">[373]</a></sup> The price increase took effect immediately for new subscribers, but would be delayed for two years for existing members. Netflix applied similar increases in the United States (an increase of $1) and the Eurozone (an increase of €1). According to <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Forbes (magazine)">Forbes</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">[374]</a></sup> "Netflix can add roughly $500 million in annual incremental revenues in the U.S. alone by 2017 with this move" and "roughly $200–250 million in incremental revenues from price changes in international markets". However, Reuters' Felix Salmon is critical about Netflix's financial future, noting that "any time that Netflix builds up a profit margin, the studios will simply raise their prices until that margin disappears".<sup id="cite_ref-Problem_375-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Problem-375">[375]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2016">2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: 2016" data-section="35" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In April 2016, Netflix announced it would be ending a loyalty rate in certain countries for subscribers who were continuously subscribed before price rises.<sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">[376]</a></sup> Netflix spent about $5 billion on original content in 2016;<sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">[377]</a></sup> this compares to a 2015 revenue of US$6.77 billion (2015).<sup id="cite_ref-FY_378-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FY-378">[378]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(14)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Criticism" data-section="36" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-14 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-14">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Netflix" title="Criticism of Netflix">Criticism of Netflix</a></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Accessibility">Accessibility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Accessibility" data-section="37" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2011, Netflix was sued by the <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_the_Deaf_(United_States)" title="National Association of the Deaf (United States)">U.S. National Association of the Deaf</a> for not providing <a href="/wiki/Closed_captioning" title="Closed captioning">captioning</a> for the deaf or hard of hearing on all of its content, citing the <a href="/wiki/Americans_with_Disabilities_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Americans with Disabilities Act">Americans with Disabilities Act</a>. Netflix later agreed to a settlement, where it would caption its entire library by 2014, and by 2016, have captioning available for new content within seven days of release.<sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">[379]</a></sup> In an <a href="/wiki/Non-publication_of_legal_opinions_in_the_United_States" title="Non-publication of legal opinions in the United States">unpublished decision</a> issued 2015, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Ninth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit">Ninth Circuit Court of Appeals</a> ruled that the ADA did not apply to Netflix in this case, as it is "not connected to any actual, physical place".<sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">[380]</a></sup> Netflix has continued to face criticism from disability rights supporters over the quality of captioning on some of its content.<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">[381]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">[382]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadband_and_energy_consumption">Broadband and energy consumption</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Broadband and energy consumption" data-section="38" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On March 18, 2020, <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Breton" title="Thierry Breton">Thierry Breton</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_Internal_Market_and_Services" title="European Commissioner for Internal Market and Services">European Commissioner for Internal Market and Services</a> urged streaming services including Netflix to cut back their service to limit the stress on Europe's broadband networks. Confinement measures taken during the <a href="/wiki/2020_coronavirus_pandemic_in_Europe" title="2020 coronavirus pandemic in Europe">2020 coronavirus pandemic</a> increased pressure on the networks with people both working and looking for entertainment at home.<sup id="cite_ref-383" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-383">[383]</a></sup>  Netflix responded by agreeing  to reduce its streaming rate in the European Union countries by 25% for 30 days.  Although the streaming rate will be cut by 25%, users will still be able to stream in HD and 4K with reduced image quality.<sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">[384]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Content_and_partnerships">Content and partnerships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Content and partnerships" data-section="39" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Individual Netflix productions have also faced controversy over their content. Critics argued that <i><a href="/wiki/13_Reasons_Why" title="13 Reasons Why">13 Reasons Why</a></i> glamorized mental health issues such as suicide, <a href="/wiki/Depression_in_childhood_and_adolescence" title="Depression in childhood and adolescence">depression</a> and <a href="/wiki/Posttraumatic_stress_disorder" title="Posttraumatic stress disorder">post-traumatic stress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-385">[385]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-386">[386]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">[387]</a></sup> In 2018, Netflix was criticized for using stock footage from the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Lac-M%C3%A9gantic_rail_disaster" title="Lac-Mégantic rail disaster">Lac-Mégantic rail disaster</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Bird_Box_(film)" title="Bird Box (film)">Bird Box</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Travelers_(TV_series)" title="Travelers (TV series)">Travelers</a></i>. The footage was subsequently replaced.<sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">[388]</a></sup> In January 2019, Netflix censored an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Patriot_Act_with_Hasan_Minhaj" title="Patriot Act with Hasan Minhaj">Patriot Act with Hasan Minhaj</a></i> in Saudi Arabia after requests by the <a href="/wiki/Communications_and_Information_Technology_Commission_(Saudi_Arabia)" title="Communications and Information Technology Commission (Saudi Arabia)">Communications and Information Technology Commission</a>, citing material critical of the country (such as <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_bin_Salman" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohammad bin Salman">Mohammad bin Salman</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi-led military campaign in Yemen</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">[389]</a></sup></p><p>The announcement that <a href="/wiki/Gwyneth_Paltrow" title="Gwyneth Paltrow">Gwyneth Paltrow</a>'s company <a href="/wiki/Goop_(company)" title="Goop (company)">Goop</a> had partnered with Netflix led to criticism, noting that the company has frequently been criticized for making unsubstantiated claims about the effectiveness of health treatments and products that it promotes. Multiple critics argued that granting Goop access to Netflix's platform was a "win for <a href="/wiki/Pseudoscience" title="Pseudoscience">pseudoscience</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-thedailybeast_219-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thedailybeast-219">[219]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">[390]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bundel_221-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bundel-221">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ars-goopseries_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-goopseries-218">[218]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_distribution_model">Film distribution model</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Film distribution model" data-section="40" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Netflix's distribution model for original films has led to conflicts with the legacy film industry. Some cinemas have refused to screen films distributed theatrically by Netflix (primarily to ensure awards eligibility), as it defies the standard three-month <a href="/wiki/Release_window" class="mw-redirect" title="Release window">release window</a>, and releases them simultaneously on its streaming platform (although <i><a href="/wiki/Roma_(2018_film)" title="Roma (2018 film)">Roma</a></i> was instead given a three-week run before being added to the streaming service). <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a>, governor of the directors branch of the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Motion_Picture_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences">Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences</a> (AMPAS), has been critical of the streaming model over the "communal", cinema experience, but later clarified his views by arguing that viewers should have access to "great stories", and be able to "find their entertainment in any form or fashion that suits them".<sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">[391]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">[392]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">[393]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">[394]</a></sup> In April 2019, AMPAS voted against the possibility of changes to the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a> eligibility criteria to account for streaming services such as Netflix, although AMPAS president <a href="/wiki/John_Bailey_(cinematographer)" title="John Bailey (cinematographer)">John Bailey</a> did state that the organization would "further study the profound changes occurring in our industry".<sup id="cite_ref-screendaily-eligibility_395-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-screendaily-eligibility-395">[395]</a></sup></p><p>In 2018, Netflix pulled out of the <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival" title="Cannes Film Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a>, in response to new rules requiring competition films to have been released in French theaters. The Cannes premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/Okja" title="Okja">Okja</a></i> in 2017 was controversial, and led to discussions over the appropriateness of films with simultaneous digital releases being screened at an event showcasing theatrical film; audience members also booed at the Netflix <a href="/wiki/Vanity_plate" title="Vanity plate">vanity plate</a> at the screening. Netflix's attempts to negotiate allowing a limited release in France were curtailed by organizers, as well as French <a href="/wiki/Cultural_exception" title="Cultural exception">cultural exception</a> law—where theatrically screened films are legally forbidden from being made available via video on-demand services until at least 36 months after their release.<sup id="cite_ref-396" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-396">[396]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-397">[397]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-398" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-398">[398]</a></sup></p><p>Beginning at the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="Toronto International Film Festival">Toronto International Film Festival</a>, films may now be restricted from screening at <a href="/wiki/Scotiabank_Theatre_Toronto" title="Scotiabank Theatre Toronto">Scotiabank Theatre Toronto</a>—one of the festival's main venues—and screened elsewhere (such as <a href="/wiki/TIFF_Bell_Lightbox" title="TIFF Bell Lightbox">TIFF Bell Lightbox</a> and other local cinemas) if distributed by a service such as Netflix. Organizers stated that the restriction was due to a policy enforced by the facility's owner and operator, <a href="/wiki/Cineplex_Entertainment" title="Cineplex Entertainment">Cineplex Entertainment</a>, requiring adherence to 3-month theatrical windows.<sup id="cite_ref-399" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-399">[399]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Tax_avoidance">Tax avoidance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Tax avoidance" data-section="41" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>According to a blog post by the <a href="/wiki/Institute_on_Taxation_and_Economic_Policy" title="Institute on Taxation and Economic Policy">Institute on Taxation and Economic Policy</a>, Netflix reported its largest ever profit in the US for 2018, but paid nothing in federal or state tax.<sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-400">[400]</a></sup> The explanation is that US Tax law allows companies to claim <a href="/wiki/Tax_credit" title="Tax credit">tax credit</a> on foreign earnings and thus avoid double taxation.<sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-401">[401]</a></sup> US Senator <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Sanders" title="Bernie Sanders">Bernie Sanders</a> has criticized Netflix for this both on Twitter <sup id="cite_ref-402" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-402">[402]</a></sup> and at a Fox News town hall event on April 15, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-403" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-403">[403]</a></sup> A spokesperson from Netflix has addressed such claims as "inaccurate", but no evidence has been provided that Netflix did pay any state or federal taxes.<sup id="cite_ref-404" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-404">[404]</a></sup></p><p>Allegations of tax evasion are also being investigated by Italian prosecutors. While Netflix doesn't have a headquarters in Italy, the prosecution claims that the digital infrastructure such as servers and cables amounts to a physical presence in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-405" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-405">[405]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Viewership_figure_claims">Viewership figure claims</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Viewership figure claims" data-section="42" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Netflix has been called out by some media organizations and competitors for only rarely and selectively releasing its ratings and viewer numbers. A notable instance of this involves the film <i><a href="/wiki/Bird_Box_(film)" title="Bird Box (film)">Bird Box</a></i>. A week after its release, Netflix claimed that it had the biggest seven-day viewing record of any of its original films at over 45 million viewers, but did not provide data to validate it.<sup id="cite_ref-406" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-406">[406]</a></sup> It also was not possible to accurately compare its week-long success to a major cultural event such as the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a> or <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a> or to a <a href="/wiki/Blockbuster_(entertainment)" title="Blockbuster (entertainment)">blockbuster</a> film run.<sup id="cite_ref-407" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-407">[407]</a></sup> In June 2019, Netflix claimed that 30,869,863 accounts watched the <a href="/wiki/Adam_Sandler" title="Adam Sandler">Adam Sandler</a>- and <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Aniston" title="Jennifer Aniston">Jennifer Aniston</a>-starring Netflix original film <i><a href="/wiki/Murder_Mystery_(film)" title="Murder Mystery (film)">Murder Mystery</a></i>, despite it being critically panned, making it the biggest "opening weekend" for a Netflix original film. If the film had been in theaters it would have made the equivalent of $556 million based on a $9 ticket price. Critics cast doubt that this number of people would have watched the film given that it would have made the film more popular than the finale of <i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones" title="Game of Thrones">Game of Thrones</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-408" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-408">[408]</a></sup></p><p>In the fourth quarter of 2019, Netflix changed the method it used to estimate viewers for a show. Prior to this, Netflix counted a viewer towards viewership if they watched 70% of the show; with the new change, a viewer need only watch two minutes of the show to count. Netflix stated the two-minute metric indicated that the viewer chose to watch the show, and thus counted in its viewership. This also eliminated factors such as length of the work, so that both short and long works would be treated equally. In a statement to shareholders, Netflix estimated this increased viewership by 35% on average.<sup id="cite_ref-409" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-409">[409]</a></sup> This new metric was criticized as commentators felt two minutes was far too little of any show to engage a viewer, and instead the move by Netflix was to artificially increase viewership to put their numbers on par with television networks and movie ticket sales, such as trying to compare viewership of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Witcher_(TV_series)" title="The Witcher (TV series)">The Witcher</a></i> with that of HBO's <i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Game of Thrones (TV series)">Game of Thrones</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-410" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-410">[410]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-411" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-411">[411]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(15)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_and_legacy">Effects and legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netflix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Effects and legacy" data-section="43" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-15 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-15">
<p>The rise of Netflix has affected the way that audiences watch televised content. Netflix's CPO Neil Hunt points out that the Internet allows users the freedom to watch shows at their own pace, so an episode does not need cliffhangers to tease the audience to keep tuning in week after week because they can just continue into the next episode.<sup id="cite_ref-412" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-412">[412]</a></sup> Netflix has allowed content creators to deviate from traditional formats that force 30-minute or 60-minute time slots once a week, which it claims gives them an advantage over networks. Their model provides a platform which allows varying run times per episode based on a storyline, eliminates the need for a week to week recap, and does not have a fixed notion of what constitutes a "season". This flexibility also allows Netflix to nurture a show until it finds its audience, unlike traditional networks which will quickly cancel a show if it is unable to maintain steady ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-413" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-413">[413]</a></sup></p><p>Netflix has strayed from the traditional necessary production of a pilot episode to establish the characters and create arbitrary cliffhangers to prove to the network that the concept of the show will be successful. Kevin Spacey spoke at the <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_International_Television_Festival" title="Edinburgh International Television Festival">Edinburgh International Television Festival</a> about how the new Netflix model was effective for the production of <i>House of Cards</i>: "Netflix was the only company that said, 'We believe in you. We've run our data, and it tells us our audience would watch this series.'" Traditional networks are unwilling to risk millions of dollars on shows without first seeing a pilot, but Spacey points out that 113 pilots were made in 2012; 35 of them were chosen to go to air, 13 were renewed, and most are gone now. The total cost of this is somewhere between $300 million and $400 million, which makes Netflix's deal for <i>House of Cards</i> extremely cost effective, according to Spacey.<sup id="cite_ref-414" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-414">[414]</a></sup> Netflix's subscription fee also eliminates the need for commercials, so they do not need to appease advertisers to fund their original content, a model similar to pay television services such as HBO and Showtime.
</p><p>The Netflix model has also affected viewers' expectations. According to a 2013 Nielsen survey, more than 60-percent of Americans said that they binge-watch shows, and nearly 8 out of 10 Americans have used technology to watch their favorite shows on their own schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-415" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-415">[415]</a></sup> Netflix has continued to release its original content by making the whole season available at once, acknowledging changing viewer habits. This allows audiences to watch episodes at a time of their choosing rather than having to watch just one episode a week at a specific scheduled time; this effectively gives its subscribers freedom and control over when to watch the next episode at their own pace.
</p>
